  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8655084-phrynne?shelf=5000-books">5000-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1746676461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1791079671529858087">This was such a pleasure to read. It is a simple story about an uncomplicated man who is required to perform some difficult tasks. He has to step way beyond his comfort zone and in doing so discovers his own inner strengths. Even better, it becomes a bit of a fairy story as he discovers he has friends he never knew about who step in and make his life better.<br/><br/>I have always enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute' title='Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevil Shute</a>'s writing. I read most of his books as a teenager when I read my way through my parent's bookshelves. Afte</span>
  <span id="freeText1791079671529858087" style="display:none">This was such a pleasure to read. It is a simple story about an uncomplicated man who is required to perform some difficult tasks. He has to step way beyond his comfort zone and in doing so discovers his own inner strengths. Even better, it becomes a bit of a fairy story as he discovers he has friends he never knew about who step in and make his life better.<br /><br />I have always enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute" title="Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevil Shute</a>'s writing. I read most of his books as a teenager when I read my way through my parent's bookshelves. After all this time I do not really know which ones I have read but I am sure I had not come across <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107300.Trustee_from_the_Toolroom" title="Trustee from the Toolroom by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">Trustee from the Toolroom</a> before. It is not a short book and it has plenty of pages of technical detail but even that, written by this author, is very readable.<br /><br />So nice to read a book with no over the top drama, no hysterics or anguish, just sensible, ordinary people making the best of their lives - with a little bit of special good luck as their reward.</span>

<div id="review_1426313953" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426313953" />
    <a title="Chrissie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/632247-chrissie"><img alt="Chrissie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321799585p2/632247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426313953?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chrissie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chrissie" href="/user/show/632247-chrissie">Chrissie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=hawaii">hawaii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=travel">travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=philo-psychol">philo-psychol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=great-britain">great-britain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=tahiti">tahiti</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426313953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9150717899153105607">Oh my, I <b>did</b> like this. It is light, but cute and fun and will make you smile. I certainly do recommend it. <br/><br/>So what is this about? On the surface it is about a Mr. Ordinary, an unpretentious little guy, but he is honest and hardworking. He is kind. He is happy with little. He doesn't need a big fancy house or a flashy job or fancy clothes. It is an adventure story too. Travel on airplanes and boats - a trip that you would not imagine! <br/><br/>There is a peculiar characteristic to this book. The details.</span>
  <span id="freeText9150717899153105607" style="display:none">Oh my, I <b>did</b> like this. It is light, but cute and fun and will make you smile. I certainly do recommend it. <br /><br />So what is this about? On the surface it is about a Mr. Ordinary, an unpretentious little guy, but he is honest and hardworking. He is kind. He is happy with little. He doesn't need a big fancy house or a flashy job or fancy clothes. It is an adventure story too. Travel on airplanes and boats - a trip that you would not imagine! <br /><br />There is a peculiar characteristic to this book. The details. Nevil Shute was an aeronautics engineer. You can tell. The book is filled with detailed descriptions of machines and mechanical gadgets - for airplanes, for boats, for lumber mills. Parts of machines - coil winders and plate fittings and gear boxes and hydraulic jacks and roller chains and sprockets and lathes and heat transfer gizmos and…. I don't know what all these things are but they sure make the story told feel thoroughly authentic. Yet you are not confused. You do understand what is going one through all the jumble of details. <br /><br />So do all the details bore you? No, because the message conveyed is about people. The message conveyed is so simple and so obvious, but one we often forget. The scenarios drawn are not believable, but they will make you smile. <br /> <br />I listened to the audiobook narrated by Frank Muller. He reads pretty darn quickly. He lavishly impersonates; let's say exaggerates the different characters. The Scott sounds very Scottish, the American very American, the women sweet, the dumb guys sounds a bit like a moron. Still this is all kind of appropriate because it makes you smile even more. It is funny because Jack, the one who is supposed to be so stupid....well, is he really? The book <b>and</b>the narration will make you smile. The two fit each other. <br /><br />This book is fun. The story is cute. I guarantee it will put a smile on your face. Do you need to smile? Go read it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9150717899153105607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer206029742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4580579978048377261">A personal note: <br/><br/>Before reading this book, my only exposure to the works of Nevil Shute had been watching the delightful movie A Town Like Alice. I used to watch that movie over and over as a kid, especially whenever my father (who has a workaholics dream job) had a little time to spend with me. Nevil Shute has always been one of his favorite authors and as such, that movie has always been a source of fond feelings. This month, I have a rare opportunity to spend time with my dad, as he's taking </span>
  <span id="freeText4580579978048377261" style="display:none">A personal note: <br /><br />Before reading this book, my only exposure to the works of Nevil Shute had been watching the delightful movie A Town Like Alice. I used to watch that movie over and over as a kid, especially whenever my father (who has a workaholics dream job) had a little time to spend with me. Nevil Shute has always been one of his favorite authors and as such, that movie has always been a source of fond feelings. This month, I have a rare opportunity to spend time with my dad, as he's taking a rare vacation to go to the Shute convention in Seattle and he wanted me to come along. So this week I started reading this book.<br /><br /><br /><br />And now, down to the review:<br /><br />From the size of Shute's books, I figured that it was going to be a light read, amusing probably, but not very engaging. Boy was I wrong! I just finished Trustee From the Tool Room and I'm going to have to start my next Shute book right away. His writing style is concise - he wastes no words and yet manages to describe things thoroughly. His characters are engaging and believable. I found them to be intelligent, with their own strengths and weaknesses. It's rare to find an author who can ensure that though his character's may know a lot in a field of their interest (engineering in this case) it does not mean that they know everything on the subject and are super-human like most books. All characters are treated with sympathy for personal faults, understanding of their limitations and pride for their strengths. Shute is quick to point out that there are many ways to overcome obstacles, and the simple act of doing your job professionally, competently and courteously can have long reaching effects on other people and help in a time of need. <br /><br />Keith Stewart is the main character - a sensible average British citizen who has never gone far in life in either distance or career. However, though he has little money and little experience outside his town and job he's quite happy. When his wealthy sister and brother-in-law ask him to take care of their daughter for a few months while they settle into a new home in Canada - he readily agrees. When they're both killed in a horrible accident, Keith finds himself the new Trustee of their fortune until his niece is old enough to claim it. When he finds out the fortune has mysteriously gone missing, cash strapped Keith must travel halfway across the world to try and recover his niece's fortune for her - no matter the danger.<br /><br />The story is written in the British fashion, understated but highly enjoyable. Even the parts that go into engineering difficulties are accessible to the average reader. I'd recommend it to anyone who enjoys relaxing reads about average people forced out of their comfort zone. Not the fastest paced novel out there, but the way Shute writes, he managed to keep me interested even so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4580579978048377261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_296988932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/296988932" />
    <a title="Jo Walton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3350560-jo-walton"><img alt="Jo Walton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333431622p2/3350560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/296988932?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo Walton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo Walton" href="/user/show/3350560-jo-walton">Jo Walton</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer296988932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18100586484136578199">You know, I love this book with all my heart, it is the story of an ordinary unassuming man going on an unusual trip and winning out because of his ordinary life in which he designs miniature engineering models and people make them. Men, that is, hmm. Anyway, it's an adorable and unusual book. Read it, you'll like it, it has SF sensibility without being SF.<br/><br/>But.<br/><br/>It's 1960. And because of what Shute takes to be the horrible socialist government in Britain, British people cannot legally take all the</span>
  <span id="freeText18100586484136578199" style="display:none">You know, I love this book with all my heart, it is the story of an ordinary unassuming man going on an unusual trip and winning out because of his ordinary life in which he designs miniature engineering models and people make them. Men, that is, hmm. Anyway, it's an adorable and unusual book. Read it, you'll like it, it has SF sensibility without being SF.<br /><br />But.<br /><br />It's 1960. And because of what Shute takes to be the horrible socialist government in Britain, British people cannot legally take all their capital (25,000 pounds, at a time where a house in London costs 2000 and 1000 a year is a reasonable private income) out of the country without being taxed on it. But the characters and the authorial voice, think this is wrong, and do it anyway, and getting it back is a lot of what the book is about. But but but -- the reason given, over and over, for getting it back, is so that Janice can have an education. Has it escaped your notice, Mr Shute, that in 1960 if Janice was bright enough to go to Oxford she could have done it without the money? That this was what the taxes were for? So not just lucky Janice but the bright kids who didn't have a rich parent could go to university? The plot doesn't work at any other time either -- in times of horrible inequality and university out of reach for ordinary people, like the 30s and oh yes, RIGHT NOW, nobody cares what rich people do with their money, they can turn it into dollars at will, so there'd be no need for it. And yes, it's great that you see how people who "raised themselves" (in class) by their own efforts are deserving, but you know why we need free education at all levels even for people whose parents didn't do that is because they're kids, they're children, even if their parents are an utter waste these are new people and all of us owe them the future because they're going to see it and we aren't. <br /><br />On the plus side, positive portrayal of non-white characters and Jews. He was really making an effort on that front.<br /><br />Nevil Shute is dead. I wasn't even born when he wrote this book. I couldn't ever have yelled at him about it. And anyway, I genuinely do love it despite the fact that reading it turns me into a raving 1944 settlement socialist.<br /><br />Also, a classic example of an utterly readable unputdownable book in which nothing happens. Well, I guess there is a shipwreck. But even so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18100586484136578199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3436894098" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3436894098" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2967061-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577653837p2/2967061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3436894098?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/2967061-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3436894098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14396347443651829588">Such an uninviting title for a terrific novel. It does fit the story and perhaps when it was written it wouldn't have been a turn off. Anyway, Nevil Shute's name came up recently and I decided to read something by him which I hadn't read yet and I'm so glad that I found this book and looked beyond the title.<br/><br/> I've read many novels by Nevil Shute and this is the first that does not take place during war time. We have the usual Shute set up with a man living his life until something happens and he </span>
  <span id="freeText14396347443651829588" style="display:none">Such an uninviting title for a terrific novel. It does fit the story and perhaps when it was written it wouldn't have been a turn off. Anyway, Nevil Shute's name came up recently and I decided to read something by him which I hadn't read yet and I'm so glad that I found this book and looked beyond the title.<br /><br /> I've read many novels by Nevil Shute and this is the first that does not take place during war time. We have the usual Shute set up with a man living his life until something happens and he must go on a journey or take on a task that is risky and way out of his comfort zone. And that is just what happens in this story. He must get to a small island somewhere off the coast of Tahiti but has no idea how to get there. He finds a plane which will take him as close as possible, which is still quite far away, hoping that there will be a boat going to or near the island soon. No such luck. He finds a drunken "sailor" who has a small boat in poor condition without a motor. Given no other options he learns navigation as quickly as possible (the sailor doesn't know navigation) and off they go. I loved this shipboard relationship. Our clever protagonist must take orders from the apparently not so clever skipper. He doesn't mind a bit and finds that the skipper knows something about sailing, he just doesn't use the usual navigational methods. Plus, our protagonist has such a positive and can-do spirit about every obstacle that comes along; he stays calm and figures out what to do whenever a situation arises (and of course situations arise this being a Shute novel). <br /><br /> I loved almost every minute of this story; I say almost because I could have done a bit less with the "toolroom" talk about building instruments and aeronautics, etc. I'll say no more so as not to spoil the story. Let's just say that I had a smile on my face while reading and after turning the last page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14396347443651829588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_109494581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109494581" />
    <a title="Jenne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26259-jenne"><img alt="Jenne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1173836583p2/26259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109494581?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenne" href="/user/show/26259-jenne">Jenne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jenne by: </span>
      Liz Hildreth
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26259-jenne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109494581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3314767276940196684">I think the reason I liked this book so much, is that like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/101334.Remainder' title='Remainder by Tom McCarthy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Remainder</a>, it's a book about logistics. A very complicated thing needs to happen (In this case, a mild-mannered engineer who has never left England needs to get to a tiny island near Tahiti) and the book is about how people find creative solutions to get it done. For some reason, I am <b>completely fascinated</b> by this kind of story. Maybe it's all the years I spent playing "initiative games" at camp?<br/><br/>This is not the best book ever written. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText3314767276940196684" style="display:none">I think the reason I liked this book so much, is that like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/101334.Remainder" title="Remainder by Tom McCarthy" rel="nofollow noopener">Remainder</a>, it's a book about logistics. A very complicated thing needs to happen (In this case, a mild-mannered engineer who has never left England needs to get to a tiny island near Tahiti) and the book is about how people find creative solutions to get it done. For some reason, I am <b>completely fascinated</b> by this kind of story. Maybe it's all the years I spent playing "initiative games" at camp?<br /><br />This is not the best book ever written. The style is kind of clunky, and the attitudes to women, ethnic groups, etc. are outdated as you might expect for a book written in 1960. <br /><br />HOWEVER, I'm giving it 5 stars because while I was reading it, I didn't want to be doing <i>anything else.</i><br /><br />Some people would also probably hate the huge sections of technical details about sailing and building miniature engines and airplane design and sawmill construction and on and on, but I actually like that kind of stuff.<br /><br />Thanks for recommending it, Liz!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3314767276940196684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_512069264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512069264" />
    <a title="Judy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3333943-judy"><img alt="Judy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267037102p2/3333943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512069264?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy" href="/user/show/3333943-judy">Judy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333943-judy?shelf=books-from-1960">books-from-1960</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333943-judy?shelf=20th-century-fiction">20th-century-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512069264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4909484929058669791">The #9 bestseller from 1960 took me completely by surprise. The title invoked boredom and also made little sense. But <i>On The Beach</i>, Shute's bestseller from 1957, had made a big impression on me and gave me hope.<br/><br/>The trustee of the title is Keith Stewart, one of those unprepossessing fellows from postwar England who bumbles along, doesn't expect much, but is an honest and honorable sort. These days he would be considered a world class nerd.<br/><br/>In his basement workshop he makes miniature models of engi</span>
  <span id="freeText4909484929058669791" style="display:none">The #9 bestseller from 1960 took me completely by surprise. The title invoked boredom and also made little sense. But <i>On The Beach</i>, Shute's bestseller from 1957, had made a big impression on me and gave me hope.<br /><br />The trustee of the title is Keith Stewart, one of those unprepossessing fellows from postwar England who bumbles along, doesn't expect much, but is an honest and honorable sort. These days he would be considered a world class nerd.<br /><br />In his basement workshop he makes miniature models of engines, clocks, motorcycles, etc, carefully milling and lathing his own machine parts. He also writes a column for a niche magazine, the "Miniature Mechanic." Though he receives letter from all over the world and conscientiously answers every one, his take home pay is as minuscule as his models. <br /><br />Then, in the way of any good story, upheaval arrives when his sister and her fairly wealthy husband perish at sea, leaving Keith and his long suffering but supremely practical wife as guardians for their nine-year-old niece. Keith is also named trustee for the little girl's inheritance which turns out to include a valuable stash of diamonds lost on a corral island near Hawaii.<br /><br />Soon enough this man who has never left England and rarely ventures from his hometown, has an adventure by air and sea the likes of which he had never imagined. Somehow, despite the unlikelihood of several coincidences, the story hooked me.<br /><br />It is one of those tales where uprightness and hard work pay off. In our current world where dishonesty pays until it doesn't, where our heroes usually turn out to be false, I fell for the heartwarming simplicity of a guy who faces hardship to do the right thing and who, because he is skilled and clever and willing to go every extra mile required, wins in the end.<br /><br />I made my husband read it. He is an engineer of sorts himself and a practical guy. It brought a tear to his one good eye, as we like to say about him when he (rarely) gets emotional, and pronounced it great. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4909484929058669791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24174171" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3002699737908876035">This is my second favorite Nevil Shute story, after "A Town Like Alice."<br/><br/>My Dad flew full-sized airplanes and sailplanes, and also model airplanes; especially small rubber-band powered "Peanut" scale airplanes. He was known among the world-wide model airplane community as the "Ol' Professor" for the informative quality he incorporated into his numerous scale model airplane designs and instructions.<br/><br/>My Dad and Keith Stewart were so alike that many of his friends would point out the similarity betwe</span>
  <span id="freeText3002699737908876035" style="display:none">This is my second favorite Nevil Shute story, after "A Town Like Alice."<br /><br />My Dad flew full-sized airplanes and sailplanes, and also model airplanes; especially small rubber-band powered "Peanut" scale airplanes. He was known among the world-wide model airplane community as the "Ol' Professor" for the informative quality he incorporated into his numerous scale model airplane designs and instructions.<br /><br />My Dad and Keith Stewart were so alike that many of his friends would point out the similarity between the two of them after they discovered this Nevil Shute tale of a supremely contented designer and model builder, who journeys from England to a deserted South Pacific atoll to keep faith with his dead sister and brother-in-law and return with his neice's inheritance from the wreckage of their sailboat.<br /><br />Like Keith Stewart, my Father was always "perfectly, supremely, happy" with the way his work and his hobbies meshed together.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6831299563053143007">My very favorite Nevil Shute novel. A seemingly simple man who writes articles about scale models must go on a quest. To say it simply, he must retrieve valuable gems from a ship-wrecked boat to support his niece. I have been looking for my own copy for years. Pick one up for me if you ever see one.<br/><br/>Update...just got the Kindle cop</span>
  <span id="freeText6831299563053143007" style="display:none">My very favorite Nevil Shute novel. A seemingly simple man who writes articles about scale models must go on a quest. To say it simply, he must retrieve valuable gems from a ship-wrecked boat to support his niece. There are many adventures on the way to Polynesia (I think) andhe discovers that his life is not so small, after all. It's a quiet novel, no villains, but such a read. I have been looking for my own copy for years. Pick one up for me if you ever see one.<br /><br />Update...just got the Kindle copy. Ever so good. I enjoyed it all the more. Go...interlibrary loan it, read it. You'll enjoy this simple tale.</span>

<div id="review_1114673410" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114673410" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/336445-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266161336p2/336445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/336445-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114673410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5518799917061557138">I loved this book! There is nothing special about it, but it tells the story of very ordinary people rising to the occasion and doing what needs to be done. What that shows about their characters, plus the detailed information about mechanical engineering and sailing and logging and international politics made it un-put-downable for me. I can't wait to read it all over again!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3484481560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3484481560" />
    <a title="Margie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4870237-margie"><img alt="Margie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528501408p2/4870237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3484481560?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margie" href="/user/show/4870237-margie">Margie</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=coronavirus-escapes">coronavirus-escapes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=island">island</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=page-turner">page-turner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=tahiti">tahiti</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870237-margie?shelf=sailing">sailing</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3484481560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16793217847605155199">Trustee From the Toolroom was Nevil Shute's last book.  It tells the tale of a mild mannered, unremarkable man who made a remarkable journey to fulfill his responsibility as trustee for his niece.<br/><br/>In addition to being a gifted writer of adventure, historical fiction, post-apocalyptic and many other novels, Shute was an engineer, a pilot, the owner of an aircraft company, a designer of secret weapons for the British during World War II, a sailor and a pilot.  All these vocations, hobbies and inter</span>
  <span id="freeText16793217847605155199" style="display:none">Trustee From the Toolroom was Nevil Shute's last book.  It tells the tale of a mild mannered, unremarkable man who made a remarkable journey to fulfill his responsibility as trustee for his niece.<br /><br />In addition to being a gifted writer of adventure, historical fiction, post-apocalyptic and many other novels, Shute was an engineer, a pilot, the owner of an aircraft company, a designer of secret weapons for the British during World War II, a sailor and a pilot.  All these vocations, hobbies and interests find a way into his books.  Even though I am not a sailor or pilot or have any engineering knowledge, I find all these elements in his books fascinating.  They never drag on too long or become boring.<br /><br />Keith Roberts, a mild mannered Scots-Englishman who loves creating miniature mechanical models and writing about them, lives with his wife, Katie, in West Ealing, England.  He  has never been outside of Britain, but is suddenly thrust into an amazing adventure, a journey to Tahiti and an outlying island in the Tuamotus to rescue a treasure of diamonds.  This book was a page turner (even though much of the help Keith got along the way seemed a bit too convenient.)<br /><br />Shute was a champion of the middle and lower classes.  You can tell he despised the class system and I think he may have had some issues with the Royal Navy as well.  He also loved telling the stories of self-made men.  In this book two American multi-millionaires, industrial titans, who started from the ground up, play prominent roles in the story.  One in particular helps Keith complete his adventure and fulfill his duty as trustee.<br /><br />This was a wonderful story of an ordinary, decent man, leading an unremarkable, quiet life, thrust into the adventure of his life and succeeding - one of Nevil Shute's best! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16793217847605155199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1919734647" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1919734647" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/362843-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497364384p2/362843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1919734647?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/362843-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/362843-jennifer?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919734647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6818913383619819421">I'm a Nevil Shute fan so my rating is really in relation to other Shute novels - I liked it but it really isn't one of my favorites. It's so methodical and detailed in it's slow progression of actions. Our hero Keith Stewart is a simple man and the book walks through every step he takes over the better part of year after his sister and brother in law are killed in a boat crash. (Actually that boat crash was a pretty good section and was a bit of a diversion from the rest of the book's tone.)<br/><br/>But </span>
  <span id="freeText6818913383619819421" style="display:none">I'm a Nevil Shute fan so my rating is really in relation to other Shute novels - I liked it but it really isn't one of my favorites. It's so methodical and detailed in it's slow progression of actions. Our hero Keith Stewart is a simple man and the book walks through every step he takes over the better part of year after his sister and brother in law are killed in a boat crash. (Actually that boat crash was a pretty good section and was a bit of a diversion from the rest of the book's tone.)<br /><br />But what I found interesting was that multiple times Shute talks about Stewart in terms of being satisfied by a simpler life without money. "He would have made more money in a toolroom progressing up from the charge-hand to the foreman; he would have made more money as an instructor in a technical college. He would not have made more happiness than he had now attained." This theme is repeated through out the book and others are aghast at how little money he makes etc. Since the action of the book is driven by his quest for a treasure that sunk with his sister's boat I wonder if this is emphasized to show that he was doing it for his niece and not out of greed or if Shute is really trying to promote a minimalist lifestyle. <br /><br />Either way, the book was enjoyable but fell a bit flat for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6818913383619819421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6319360886062131936">What a wonderful treat. In this story, people are happy and kind and reliable even though this is written at a time when the public had been through both World Wars, the Great Depression, and post-war rationing. I've seen "do what you love, the money will follow" happen to people so I don't think this story is crazy. In fact, a less exaggerated version of this is what happens systematically when society more or less functions properly instead of hyper-rewarding cheaters. <br/><br/>Accessory rant:<br/>Book crit</span>
  <span id="freeText6319360886062131936" style="display:none">What a wonderful treat. In this story, people are happy and kind and reliable even though this is written at a time when the public had been through both World Wars, the Great Depression, and post-war rationing. I've seen "do what you love, the money will follow" happen to people so I don't think this story is crazy. In fact, a less exaggerated version of this is what happens systematically when society more or less functions properly instead of hyper-rewarding cheaters. <br /><br />Accessory rant:<br />Book critics today seem to give prizes for depressing dross where everyone is whiney or evil and the "sentences are beautiful." This is all part of the surface over substance cultural disease. Nihilism and meaninglessness are not forms of sophistication. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11548647626464654709">I was lucky enough to stumble across a box containing all 24 of Nevil Shute's novels in paperback. After putting them all in copyright date order, I have been able to read my way through most of his books while "watching" him progress as a writer. Such fun!</span>

<div id="review_90369617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90369617" />
    <a title="Andrew Walter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1190645-andrew-walter"><img alt="Andrew Walter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325691961p2/1190645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90369617?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Walter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Walter" href="/user/show/1190645-andrew-walter">Andrew Walter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90369617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8996099242921955225">Recommended to me by my Dad (himself with a background in engineering) as one of Shute's best.<br/><br/>While reading this tale of quiet model engineer Keith Stewart's journey to previously unimagined parts of the globe in an attempt to recover his nieces birthright, I couldn't help feeling a little saddened throughout. It may be me spouting off, uninformed, with my higher education arts degree, but I got the impression while reading that books like this just won't be written anymore. Not due to the stren</span>
  <span id="freeText8996099242921955225" style="display:none">Recommended to me by my Dad (himself with a background in engineering) as one of Shute's best.<br /><br />While reading this tale of quiet model engineer Keith Stewart's journey to previously unimagined parts of the globe in an attempt to recover his nieces birthright, I couldn't help feeling a little saddened throughout. It may be me spouting off, uninformed, with my higher education arts degree, but I got the impression while reading that books like this just won't be written anymore. Not due to the strength of the writing (which is competent but never sets out to dazzle) but due to the combination of specialist technical detail and humanity.<br /><br />Nevil Shute was an aeronautical engineer first and a writer second, but you’ll never feel like either facet is overtly stressed at any point in this book. Today an engineer with a successful career as writer would probably be treated as a novelty, interviewed in the glossy pages of weekend supplement wearing greasy overalls and posing tongue-in-cheek with his big tools. <br /><br />Keith Stewart is not only an un-cynical and modest master of his craft, he is also unconcerned with his progression up any imagined ladder of life. Despite this, he is loved worldwide for his contributions to his hobby, a fact that is expedient to his daunting task and which at one point arguably keeps him from becoming an international prisoner. The whole tone of the way this quiet little man is presented by Shute seemed very at odds with 21st century Britain, with its panicky squawking about unemployment rates, "Mickey Mouse degrees", aggressive careerism and a government with a misplaced obsessive attitude to "social mobility".<br /><br />The most remarkable part in this story, and one that finely epitomises how I feel about it, is Keith’s construction of some toy duck eggs for his bereaved niece. I’ve never before read a piece of writing where the exact, precise description of metalworking techniques is used to evoke emotion, but it was extremely touching, and nicely portrays Shute’s attitude toward the artisan, and to skilled work in general. Keith and his wife Katie reminded me a bit of some of Raymond Briggs’ couples at some points- they are uncomplicated yet sensible, without ever being portrayed in a sentimental or mawkish manner.<br /><br />It could be argued that the book is thin on plot, and it is essentially little more than a travelogue, but the strength of having such a likeable main character means it is never a chore. I'd recommend it to anybody who wants refreshingly unpretentious story with very human characters. If I’ve made it sound like a period piece that isn’t my intention, but like I said, I find it hard to believe books like this will be written for a while.<br /><br />PS- I've read a few reviews complaining about lengthy passages of technical and maritime language. Not only does this make up a very small part of the book, it's also quite a crucial aspect of the story. Simple answer-LOOK IT UP.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8996099242921955225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2887852" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2887852" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/180908-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184048097p2/180908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2887852?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/180908-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180908-tatiana?shelf=contemporaryfiction">contemporaryfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2887852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9574185547759310039">In keeping with my rereading of favorite books lately, I just finished this one, and I loved it more than ever. Shute is such a great guy. His characters are almost always very ordinary people who just happen to be really good, kind, and amiable. I think most people actually are, really, just we don't hear about them so much. Keith Stewart is no exception. He has to make a trip to a small island in the Pacific, and he hasn't got much money, because his job doesn't pay much. What he does is desig</span>
  <span id="freeText9574185547759310039" style="display:none">In keeping with my rereading of favorite books lately, I just finished this one, and I loved it more than ever. Shute is such a great guy. His characters are almost always very ordinary people who just happen to be really good, kind, and amiable. I think most people actually are, really, just we don't hear about them so much. Keith Stewart is no exception. He has to make a trip to a small island in the Pacific, and he hasn't got much money, because his job doesn't pay much. What he does is design and build tiny model engines and machines of various types, and write articles about them for a magazine called The Miniature Mechanic. <br /><br />But it turns out that strategically placed people all around the world happen to read and enjoy his articles, and make their own model engines to his design. Those who don't happen to know about him already, instantly admire his tiny generating set that he brought along and brings out and runs for people. It sounds sort of silly, but it's all quite normal and believable and real. There actually was such a magazine published in England and the character is modeled after a real man who wrote for that journal. <br /><br />Keith goes along in that way and manages through difficulties to make it to the island. He's able to achieve his goal for the sake of his little niece. The one part that feels a bit false is the character of the niece. She doesn't seem like a real little girl to me. But the men, the airplanes, boats, sailing, flying, and building of the models is all completely true to life. I love that Nevil Shute will never lead me astray on any such things. You can count on him completely in that regard.<br /><br />Read today the sexism and racism pops out, showing us how much things have changed for the better since the time when this was written. Shute was quite progressive for his time, I think. "I would say he is a Jew, and a very good one", "They had no other choice if they wanted to keep a man in charge of the plant", some of his phrases bring me up short. I suppose one could read them today as patronizing. But for his time he's quite open minded and accepting of all sorts of people. I think he would have been a great person to know. I wish I had met him, but he was my grandparents age, or older, and he died not long after I was born. Still I can't think of any author I'd like more to have as a friend. <br /><br />Up next: The Legacy</span>
  <a data-text-id="9574185547759310039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_221922577" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221922577" />
    <a title="Arcadius" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6596962-arcadius"><img alt="Arcadius" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318889467p2/6596962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221922577?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arcadius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arcadius" href="/user/show/6596962-arcadius">Arcadius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099529989" href="/book/show/6084753-trustee-from-the-toolroom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6596962-arcadius?shelf=g-misc-geog">g-misc-geog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221922577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5067114494563780167"><br/>It's not great literature, and doesn't pretend to be, but Shute reminds us just how well made and how well written mainstream, no-formula, no-gimmicks, popular fiction can be. Or at least could be.<br/><br/>Like most authors, Shute was at his best writing about what he knew, and what he knew more about than anything else were engineering (his career) and sailing (his passion). Both feature hugely in this highly unusual story about a humble, self-effacing but great-hearted little man who overcomes all obst</span>
  <span id="freeText5067114494563780167" style="display:none"><br />It's not great literature, and doesn't pretend to be, but Shute reminds us just how well made and how well written mainstream, no-formula, no-gimmicks, popular fiction can be. Or at least could be.<br /><br />Like most authors, Shute was at his best writing about what he knew, and what he knew more about than anything else were engineering (his career) and sailing (his passion). Both feature hugely in this highly unusual story about a humble, self-effacing but great-hearted little man who overcomes all obstacles to pursue his self-imposed duty across half the world. In the end, virtue gets its reward and we can all close the book with a warm inner glow.<br /><br />Except, of course, that this is life as we want it to be, not as it is. 'Trustee' can't escape a charge of fundamental sentimentalism, and this precludes it from any claim to literary status. Otoh, we're expected to put up with Dickens' nonsense because of his writerly qualities and the other good things he has to offer, and there's no doubt that Shute has a great deal to offer as well. In the first place, he is a masterly story-teller - almost as good as Somerset Maugham, I would say. Secondly, he has the personal knowledge and writing skill to tackle subjects that seldom make it into fiction. I never thought I could endure reading so much about mechanical engineering in a novel, still less find it thoroughly absorbing. He is excellent on the pride and quiet passion of a skilled artisan for his craft, and on the international Masonic camaraderie of fellow hobby-enthusiasts. Above all, he writes superbly about the sea. Chapter 2, about the yacht caught in a tropical storm (the episode which kick-starts the story proper) is utterly gripping - an inspired piece of writing - and would certainly make it into any anthology of sea stories edited by me.<br /><br />Despite the leisurely pace, I cracked through this in a single weekend (a lot faster than I usually read) and enjoyed it immensely. Anyone interested in discovering Nevil Shute could do a lot worse for their starting point.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5067114494563780167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_876113082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/876113082" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7814046-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329615283p2/7814046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/876113082?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/7814046-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7814046-sam?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer876113082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7943265908341021911">What happens when a mild-mannered British retiree with a love for making small models and a command of mechanical principals must go into the wide-world in order to help his family? Well sex, explosions, death, and political intrigue certainly do NOT ensue but you do get a great story of a simple man choosing to step far outside of his comfort zone in order to help the ones he loves. <br/><br/>My father is a similar sort of man, the type that can still quote and apply foundational math and scientific theo</span>
  <span id="freeText7943265908341021911" style="display:none">What happens when a mild-mannered British retiree with a love for making small models and a command of mechanical principals must go into the wide-world in order to help his family? Well sex, explosions, death, and political intrigue certainly do NOT ensue but you do get a great story of a simple man choosing to step far outside of his comfort zone in order to help the ones he loves. <br /><br />My father is a similar sort of man, the type that can still quote and apply foundational math and scientific theorems that most of us forgot 2 seconds after the final exam, who like nothing better than to sit quietly and work on a model or read a book, and eat a sandwich at home. <br /><br />This book flows smoothly and is surprisingly engaging, I read it all in one day; perhaps it's a bit too neat and tidy. However, some great stories don't require shock and awe, complex build-ups and twists, or tragically flawed characters, they just need an everyday, ordinary, hero. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7943265908341021911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1275993699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1275993699" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4380068-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600374592p2/4380068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1275993699?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/4380068-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780330023078" href="/book/show/2332256.Trustee_From_The_Toolroom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4380068-bill?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4380068-bill?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1275993699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4430110143956143733">Reading a new (only for me as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute' title='Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevil Shute</a> has been dead since 1960) book by Shute is like putting on a cardigan, comfy pj's and slippers and cozying up on the couch. It's comforting, even though astounding things can happen. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107300.Trustee_from_the_Toolroom' title='Trustee from the Toolroom by Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'>Trustee from the Toolroom</a> was Shute's last book. As soon as I started reading it, I fell comfortably into the fantastic world that he created for my reading enjoyment.<br/>Like many of Shute's stories, it focuses on a normal, unassuming man (or woman) who finds him/ herself invol</span>
  <span id="freeText4430110143956143733" style="display:none">Reading a new (only for me as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute" title="Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevil Shute</a> has been dead since 1960) book by Shute is like putting on a cardigan, comfy pj's and slippers and cozying up on the couch. It's comforting, even though astounding things can happen. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107300.Trustee_from_the_Toolroom" title="Trustee from the Toolroom by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">Trustee from the Toolroom</a> was Shute's last book. As soon as I started reading it, I fell comfortably into the fantastic world that he created for my reading enjoyment.<br />Like many of Shute's stories, it focuses on a normal, unassuming man (or woman) who finds him/ herself involved in a situation so far out of his comfort zone that you find yourself following him, holding your breath to see how it will resolve. Now, I'm not saying that it's page after page of heart-stopping action. Because it isn't that. It's just that you find yourself amazed at how this mild-mannered person deals with this situation so out of his comfort zone.<br />Keith Stewart is a middle-aged Englishman living in London in the 1960's. Many years ago he gave up his wartime job as a rigger at an aircraft factory and now works from home, creating miniature engines and such and writing articles for a magazine called Miniature Mechanic. The magazine is shipped to people around the world who try to create Keith's designs and correspond with him. He makes little money and his wife makes a bit more so they can live a relatively comfortable life, nothing extravagant. They have never really traveled and live very insular lives.<br />Keith sister, Jo and her husband, an ex-Navy officer have decided to travel by sailing boat to Vancouver. They ask Keith and Katie to look after their young daughter, Janice until they get settled. They die on the way. So that's the basic story, except that as well, they have designated Keith and Katie as trustees to their daughter. They had Keith install a jewelry box in concrete in the hull of their ship; Janice's inheritance. Keith decides that if they are to ensure Janice the life she deserves, he needs to get the jewels.<br />This leads to Keith journeying to Tahiti, with little to no money to try and achieve his aim. This is the crux of this fascinating story. There are so many rich elements that develop. Keith might seem an ordinary man who lives on his street, but we gradually discover hidden elements to him that make him more and more interesting and also links to so many people around the world, that even he doesn't realize. Like all of the other stories by Shute that I've read, I was instantly drawn into the characters and the story and ultimately so satisfied with the ending. If you've never read anything by Shute, you are missing out on one of the great story tellers. (4 stars) </span>
  <a data-text-id="4430110143956143733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1236507935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1236507935" />
    <a title="Madhulika Liddle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16294266-madhulika-liddle"><img alt="Madhulika Liddle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517826893p2/16294266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1236507935?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madhulika Liddle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madhulika Liddle" href="/user/show/16294266-madhulika-liddle">Madhulika Liddle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1236507935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6061821356587509632">Keith Stewart is a middle-aged mechanic who has given up the daily grind of a job to make mechanical models—for the joy he derives from them, and for the meagre income they bring him from the magazine <i>Miniature Mechanics</i>, for which he writes articles. He and his wife Katie (a store employee) lead a quiet, uneventful life. Very unlike Keith's sister Jo, married to an ex-naval officer, John Dermott. Jo and John lead far more flamboyant, exciting lives, and having decided one day to migrate to Cana</span>
  <span id="freeText6061821356587509632" style="display:none">Keith Stewart is a middle-aged mechanic who has given up the daily grind of a job to make mechanical models—for the joy he derives from them, and for the meagre income they bring him from the magazine <i>Miniature Mechanics</i>, for which he writes articles. He and his wife Katie (a store employee) lead a quiet, uneventful life. Very unlike Keith's sister Jo, married to an ex-naval officer, John Dermott. Jo and John lead far more flamboyant, exciting lives, and having decided one day to migrate to Canada, ask Keith and Katie to look after their 10-year old daughter Janice for the few months she will be in Britain while her parents sail in their little yacht all the way to Vancouver. <br /><br />Before they embark on the voyage, however, John turns to Keith for help. Firstly, John and Jo want Keith to be the trustee for Janice should anything happen to her parents. Keith agrees. Secondly, they own a jewel box (filled, John explains, with Jo's jewels, which she is legally not allowed to take out of the country), and he wants Keith to help him fix the box—encased in concrete—to the boat's engine, so that they can smuggle it out without anybody being the wiser. Keith obliges...<br /><br />... And, a few weeks later, learns that Jo and John’s yacht has been wrecked. They were caught in a storm in the Pacific, and their bodies have been washed up, identified and buried. Their solicitor informs Keith, and informs him too that Janice's inheritance is pitifully small—her parents' bank accounts hold less than £100 between them. Some digging into documents reveals that the Dermotts had converted the bulk of their fortune into diamonds; Keith concludes that these were in the box he helped hide, and which should still be there in the wreck. So, aware that he owes it to Janice to retrieve those diamonds, Keith sets out. A man who’s never been outside England, a man with just about £100 to his (and Katie’s) name. A man who’s lived a very secluded, quiet life. He goes off, to a remote island in the Pacific, in search of diamonds. <br /><br /><i>Trustee From the Toolroom</i> is an adventure story—but a heart-warming, never really high-adrenaline style of adventure. This is a story about human relationships, about how completely unconnected people can help each other out of simple humanity; how a good turn deserves another. It’s sweet (but never syrupy), touching, funny (especially the sections relating to the delightfully eccentric Jack Donnelly), absorbing book about a man’s solo quest which turns into a group effort. <br /><br /><i>And</i> it has one of the most likeable protagonists I’ve ever encountered: <i>“… an honest little man of lower-middle-class suburban type, content to go along upon a miserable salary for the sake of doing the work he loved…”</i>. Keith Stewart is not handsome, or witty or heroic in the usual sense of the word. But he’s a wonderfully likeable man, the sort of character who does that little bit to help restore your faith in mankind. This book is much like him: gentle, likeable, warm and friendly. <br /><br />Personally, I could have done with a little less detail on the technical front (I’m woefully bad at anything to do with physics or related disciplines, so much of this went completely over my head), but still. A good introduction, as far as I’m concerned, to the work of Nevil Shute. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6061821356587509632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I read this many years ago as a teenager and it has been one of my go-to books when stress is at a maximum and sleep at a minimum. I love the story although feel particularly for the adventurous couple who are shipwrecked in the first couple of chapters. The writer never judges only steers the story and lets you decide. A deft light touch with interesting characters that wins out in the end. Always a joy. </span>

<div id="review_650781489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650781489" />
    <a title="Toi Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11540487-toi-thomas"><img alt="Toi Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983638p2/11540487.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781461812357" href="/book/show/17228674-trustee-from-the-toolroom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11540487-toi-thomas?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11540487-toi-thomas?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11540487-toi-thomas?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650781489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11672013228006593187">I really enjoyed this story when it wasn’t making me angry (more on this later), but then I just have anger issues to begin with. This is a really simple and sweet clever story about a man who’s willing to go to great lengths to keep his word- and what’s not to like about that. <br/><br/>The story of Keith Stewart describes the rare instance of a man finding true peace and contentment in his life, career, and relationships. For Keith, the whole world revolves around his workshop and the work he does there</span>
  <span id="freeText11672013228006593187" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this story when it wasn’t making me angry (more on this later), but then I just have anger issues to begin with. This is a really simple and sweet clever story about a man who’s willing to go to great lengths to keep his word- and what’s not to like about that. <br /><br />The story of Keith Stewart describes the rare instance of a man finding true peace and contentment in his life, career, and relationships. For Keith, the whole world revolves around his workshop and the work he does there writing for a magazine, but he’s no hermit. The one thing he finds that’s more important to him than his work is his word and his love for his family. When Keith finds himself the new guardian of his young niece and the trustee to her would be inheritance, he makes it his life’s purpose to secure a fine future for his new charge, despite not having the means to do so (here’s where I get angry). <br /><br />As wonderful and miraculous as this story is, Keith’s adventure never would have taken place if someone living comfortably above his station had simply acknowledge and compensated him for what he was truly worth…that’s all I’ll say about that. <br /><br />The story is told with almost manual precision, but the author’s style and flare with words keeps you pulled into the story. It’s not a fast pace action packed chronicle of a great adventure, but it is indeed a great adventure. Keith literally goes on a journey around the world trying to retrieve a modern day treasure. He ends up traveling by bus, train, plane, boat, ship, and even helicopter while encountering a great number of interesting characters along the way. To help Keith along on his journey is his forever honest and cheery disposition, his masterful mind, and his unexpected fame. This is a different kind of underdog story where there is no real favorite, just one man with a purpose fighting against a plethora of obstacles. The reader has no choice but to root for Keith all the way home. <br /><br />This was a wonderful book to listen to, perfect for my drive home. There is a lot of technical engineer talk that may or may not be interesting to readers (or listeners), but I don’t feel it took away from the overall story. Though I can’t imagine a child or teenager having the temperament for this kind of book, I’d recommend it to anyone else. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11672013228006593187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27486476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14476743136437147119">I see my score is a little below the average for this book. Hmm.<br/><br/>I've read one other <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute' title='Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'> Nevil Shute</a> book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107301.A_Town_Like_Alice' title='A Town Like Alice by Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'> A Town Like Alice</a> which I liked very much. I was drawn in from the beginning and really enjoyed it. Though it was more like two or three distinct books about the same character.<br/><br/>This one was a better, more cohesive story probably; but it was so filled with arcana (how to make a 1:20 scale generator with reduction gears, how to tack a jib and heave-to) that entire pages at a time would be "blah </span>
  <span id="freeText14476743136437147119" style="display:none">I see my score is a little below the average for this book. Hmm.<br /><br />I've read one other <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute" title="Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nevil Shute</a> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107301.A_Town_Like_Alice" title="A Town Like Alice by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Town Like Alice</a> which I liked very much. I was drawn in from the beginning and really enjoyed it. Though it was more like two or three distinct books about the same character.<br /><br />This one was a better, more cohesive story probably; but it was so filled with arcana (how to make a 1:20 scale generator with reduction gears, how to tack a jib and heave-to) that entire pages at a time would be "blah blah blah" for me. I read them anyway, every word, but didn't get much. For someone who is an engineer, builds scale models, or sails, I bet this would be a fascinating book. Come to think of it the flying part didn't bother me so much, but if I hadn't been the copilot on so many of my father's flights that might have been "blah blah blah" as well.<br /><br />But the main character Keith Stewart is immediately and completely likeable, and a lot of the other characters are wonderfully drawn and feel like friends, too. Some seem to have a bit part during their section, only to become unexpectedly important later on.<br /><br />The best part of the storyline is the way that Keith's long life of good deeds and honest, hard work come back around to him in a gargantuan dose of good karma. And bless him, in the middle of finally getting what he deserves, he's still so intent on helping others and being of use, he doesn't realize what's right in front of him. *bless*</span>
  <a data-text-id="14476743136437147119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
